Add members with specific names\n        for name, mtype in member_names.items():\n            info = tarfile.TarInfo(name)\n            if mtype == 'dir':\n                info.type = tarfile.DIRTYPE\n                tar.addfile(info)\n            else:\n                content = b'test'\n                info.size = len(content)\n                tar.addfile(info, BytesIO(content))\n\n\ndef build_ansible_cache(tar_file):\n    \"\"\"\n    Simulate how ansible builds the custom normalized cache.\n    Uses removesuffix to strip trailing path separators.\n    \"\"\"\n    cache = {}\n    for m in tar_file.getmembers():\n        # This is what ansible does (from the code at line 1609)\n        normalized_name = m.name.removesuffix(os.path.sep)\n        cache[normalized_name] = m\n    return cache\n\n\ndef test_custom_cache_fragility_with_duplicate_keys():\n    \"\"\"\n    Test that the custom cache has fragility when multiple members normalize to same key.\n\n    This demonstrates the core issue: if a tar has both \"plugins\" and \"plugins/\"\n    (which could theoretically happen), the cache dict would only retain one.\n    \"\"\"\n    with tempfile.TemporaryDirectory() as tmpdir:\n        tar_path = os.path.join(tmpdir, 'test.tar.gz')\n\n        # Create a tar with directories that have varying formats\n        members_to_add = {\n            'plugins': 'dir',\n            'plugins/modules': 'dir',\n            'plugins/modules/test.py': 'file',\n            'roles': 'dir',\n            'roles/myrole': 'dir',\n        }\n\n        create_collection_tar_with_specific_members(tar_path, members_to_add)\n\n        with tarfile.open(tar_path, mode='r') as tar:\n            # The lookups that extraction code performs\n            lookups_needed = ['plugins', 'plugins/modules', 'roles', 'roles/myrole']\n\n            # Method 1: Custom cache (ansible current approach)\n            cache = build_ansible_cache(tar)\n            cache_results = []\n            for lookup in lookups_needed:\n                try:\n                    m = cache[lookup]\n                    cache_results.append((lookup, True, m.name))\n                except KeyError:\n                    cache_results.append((lookup, False, None))\n\n            # Method 2: Standard API (more reliable)\n            api_results = []\n            for lookup in lookups_needed:\n                try:\n                    m = tar.getmember(lookup)\n                    api_results.append((lookup, True, m.name))\n                except KeyError:\n                    api_results.append((lookup, False, None))\n\n            print(\"Custom Cache Results:\")\n            for lookup, success, member_name in cache_results:\n                status = \"✓\" if success else \"✗\"\n                print(f\"  {status} {lookup!r}: {member_name!r if success else 'NOT FOUND'}\")\n\n            print(\"\\nStandard API Results:\")\n            for lookup, success, member_name in api_results:\n                status = \"✓\" if success else \"✗\"\n                print(f\"  {status} {lookup!r}: {member_name!r if success else 'NOT FOUND'}\")\n\n            cache_success = all(success for _, success, _ in cache_results)\n            api_success = all(success for _, success, _ in api_results)\n\n            print(f\"\\nCache: {'✓ All lookups succeeded' if cache_success else '✗ Some lookups failed'}\")\n            print(f\"API:   {'✓ All lookups succeeded' if api_success else '✗ Some lookups failed'}\")\n\n            return api_success  # Create FILES.json\n        files = {\n            'files': [\n                {'name': '.', 'ftype': 'dir', 'chksum_type': None, 'chksum_sha256': None},\n            ],\n            'format': 1,\n        }\n        files_json = json.dumps(files).encode()\n        fi = tarfile.TarInfo('FILES.json')\n        fi.size = len(files_json)\n        tar.addfile(fi, BytesIO(files_json))\n\n        # Add members with specific names\n        for name, mtype in member_names.items():\n            info = tarfile.TarInfo(name)\n            if mtype == 'dir':\n                info.type = tarfile.DIRTYPE\n                tar.addfile(info)\n            else:\n                content = b'test'\n                info.size = len(content)\n                tar.addfile(info, BytesIO(content))\n\n\ndef build_ansible_cache(tar_file):\n    \"\"\"\n    Simulate how ansible builds the custom normalized cache.\n    Uses removesuffix to strip trailing path separators.\n    \"\"\"\n    cache = {}\n    for m in tar_file.getmembers():\n        # The custom cache:\n\n1. Strips trailing path separators from directory member names using removesuffix()\n2. Caches members in a private _ansible_normalized_cache attribute\n3. This approach is fragile because it assumes all directory lookups will be\n   normalized the same way\n\nThe issue occurs when:\n- A tar archive stores directory entries with specific member names\n- The extraction code looks them up using removesuffix() normalization\n- If any lookup uses a different form or if there are edge cases with member\n  storage, the lookup can fail\n\nThe fix is to use the standard tarfile.getmember() API which handles member\nlookups correctly without fragile custom normalization.\n\nRelated Python issue: https://bugs.python.org/issue47231 (now fixed in modern Python)\n\"\"\"\n\nimport json\nimport os\nimport sys\nimport tarfile\nimport tempfile\nfrom io import BytesIO\n\n# Test if we can import the actual ansible code\ntry:\n    sys.path.insert(0, '/app/lib')\n    from ansible.galaxy.collection import install_artifact\n    from ansible.utils.sentinel import Sentinel\n    HAS_ANSIBLE = True\nexcept ImportError as e:\n    print(f\"Warning: Could not import ansible modules: {e}\")\n    HAS_ANSIBLE = False\n\n\ndef create_minimal_collection_tar(tar_path, dir_with_trailing_sep=False):\n    \"\"\"\n    Create a minimal test collection tar file.\n\n    When dir_with_trailing_sep=True, directory entries will have trailing separators.\n    This is the edge case that can trigger bugs in the custom cache approach.\n    \"\"\"\n    with tarfile.open(tar_path, mode='w:gz') as tar:\n        # Update manifest with correct hash\n        manifest_json = json.dumps(manifest, indent=2).encode('utf-8')\n        manifest_info = tarfile.TarInfo('MANIFEST.json')\n        manifest_info.size = len(manifest_json)\n        tar.addfile(manifest_info, BytesIO(manifest_json))\n\n        # Add FILES.json\n        files_info = tarfile.TarInfo('FILES.json')\n        files_info.size = len(files_json)\n        tar.addfile(files_info, BytesIO(files_json))\n\n        # Add directory entries\n        # Create directories WITHOUT trailing separators (canonical form)\n            plugins_dir = tarfile.TarInfo('plugins')\n            plugins_dir.type = tarfile.DIRTYPE\n            tar.addfile(plugins_dir)\n\n            modules_dir = tarfile.TarInfo('plugins/modules')\n            modules_dir.type = tarfile.DIRTYPE\n            tar.addfile(modules_dir)\n\n        # Create MANIFEST.json\n        manifest = {\n            'collection_info': {\n                'namespace': 'test',\n                'name': 'collection',\n                'version': '1.0.0',\n                'authors': ['test'],\n                'readme': 'README.md',\n                'tags': [],\n                'description': 'Test',\n                'license': ['GPL-3.0-or-later'],\n                'license_file': None,\n                'dependencies': {},\n                'repository': None,\n                'documentation': None,\n                'homepage': None,\n                'issues': None,\n            },\n            'file_manifest_file': {\n                'name': 'FILES.json',\n                'ftype': 'file',\n                'chksum_type': 'sha256',\n                'chksum_sha256': 'dummy',\n                'format': 1,\n            },\n            'format': 1,\n        }\n        manifest_json = json.dumps(manifest).encode()\n        mi = tarfile.TarInfo('MANIFEST.json')\n        mi.size = len(manifest_json)\n        tar.addfile(mi, BytesIO(manifest_json))\n\n        # Create FILES.json\n        files = {\n            'files': [\n                {'name': '.', 'ftype': 'dir', 'chksum_type': None, 'chksum_sha256': None},\n            ],\n            'format': 1,\n        }\n        files_json = json.dumps(files).encode()\n        fi = tarfile.TarInfo('FILES.json')\n        fi.size = len(files_json)\n        tar.addfile(fi, BytesIO(files_json))\n\n        # Add members with specific names\n        for name, mtype in member_names.items():\n            info = tarfile.TarInfo(name)\n            if mtype == 'dir':\n                info.type = tarfile.DIRTYPE\n                tar.addfile(info)\n            else:\n                content = b'test'\n                info.size = len(content)\n                tar.addfile(info, BytesIO(content))\n\n\ndef build_ansible_cache(tar_file):\n    \"\"\"\n    Simulate how ansible builds the custom normalized cache.\n    Uses removesuffix to strip trailing path separators.\n    \"\"\"\n    cache = {}\n    for m in tar_file.getmembers():\n        # This is what ansible does (from the code at line 1609)\n        normalized_name = m.name.removesuffix(os.path.sep)\n        cache[normalized_name] = m\n    return cache\n\n\ndef test_custom_cache_fragility_with_duplicate_keys():\n    \"\"\"\n    Test that the custom cache has fragility when multiple members normalize to same key.\n\n    This demonstrates the core issue: if a tar has both \"plugins\" and \"plugins/\"\n    (which could theoretically happen), the cache dict would only retain one.\n    \"\"\"\n    with tempfile.TemporaryDirectory() as tmpdir:\n        tar_path = os.path.join(tmpdir, 'test.tar.gz')\n\n        # Create tar with both forms of a directory (simulating an edge case)\n        # While tarfile normalizes this, some tar implementations or edge cases might not\n        with tarfile.open(tar_path, mode='w:gz') as tar:\n            # Add basic files\n            manifest = {\n                'collection_info': {'namespace': 'test', 'name': 'coll', 'version': '1.0.0',\n                                  'authors': ['test'], 'readme': 'README.md', 'tags': [],\n                                  'description': 'Test', 'license': ['GPL-3.0-or-later'],\n                                  'license_file': None, 'dependencies': {}, 'repository': None,\n                                  'documentation': None, 'homepage': None, 'issues': None},\n                'file_manifest_file': {'name': 'FILES.json', 'ftype': 'file', 'chksum_type': 'sha256',\n                                      'chksum_sha256': 'dummy', 'format': 1},\n                'format': 1,\n            }\n            manifest_json = json.dumps(manifest).encode()\n            mi = tarfile.TarInfo('MANIFEST.json')\n            mi.size = len(manifest_json)\n            tar.addfile(mi, BytesIO(manifest_json))\n\n            files = {'files': [{'name': '.', 'ftype': 'dir', 'chksum_type': None, 'chksum_sha256': None},\n                             {'name': 'plugins', 'ftype': 'dir', 'chksum_type': None, 'chksum_sha256': None}],\n                    'format': 1}\n            files_json = json.dumps(files).encode()\n            fi = tarfile.TarInfo('FILES.json')\n            fi.size = len(files_json)\n            tar.addfile(fi, BytesIO(files_json))\n\n            # Add a directory - this is the entry that will be looked up\n            plugins_dir = tarfile.TarInfo('plugins')\n            plugins_dir.type = tarfile.DIRTYPE\n            tar.addfile(plugins_dir)\n\n        with tarfile.open(tar_path, mode='r') as tar:\n            members = tar.getmembers()\n            print(\"Tar members:\")\n            for m in members:\n                print(f\"  {m.name!r} - isdir={m.isdir()}\")\n\n            # Build the ansible cache\n            cache = build_ansible_cache(tar)\n            print(\"\\nCustom cache (ansible approach):\")\n            for key, member in cache.items():\n                if member.isdir():\n                    print(f\"  cache[{key!r}] = {member.name!r}\")\n\n            # Try lookup as ansible would\n            try:\n                member = cache['plugins']\n                assert member.isdir()\n                print(f\"\\n✓ Cache lookup succeeded for 'plugins'\")\n                return True\n            except KeyError:\n                print(f\"\\n✗ Cache lookup failed for 'plugins'\")\n                return False\n\n\ndef test_standard_api_vs_custom_cache_consistency():\n    \"\"\"\n    Demonstrate that standard tarfile API is more reliable than custom cache.\n\n    The standard API handles member lookup without needing fragile normalization.\n    \"\"\"\n    with tempfile.TemporaryDirectory() as tmpdir:\n        tar_path = os.path.join(tmpdir, 'test.tar.gz')\n\n        # Create a tar with directories that have varying formats\n        members_to_add = {\n            'plugins': 'dir',\n            'plugins/modules': 'dir',\n            'plugins/modules/test.py': 'file',\n            'roles': 'dir',\n            'roles/myrole': 'dir',\n        }\n\n        create_collection_tar_with_specific_members(tar_path, members_to_add)\n\n        with tarfile.open(tar_path, mode='r') as tar:\n            # The lookups that extraction code performs\n            lookups_needed = ['plugins', 'plugins/modules', 'roles', 'roles/myrole']\n\n            # Method 1: Custom cache (ansible current approach)\n            cache = build_ansible_cache(tar)\n            cache_results = []\n            for lookup in lookups_needed:\n                try:\n                    m = cache[lookup]\n                    cache_results.append((lookup, True, m.name))\n                except KeyError:\n                    cache_results.append((lookup, False, None))\n\n            # Method 2: Standard API (more reliable)\n            api_results = []\n            for lookup in lookups_needed:\n                try:\n                    m = tar.getmember(lookup)\n                    api_results.append((lookup, True, m.name))\n                except KeyError:\n                    api_results.append((lookup, False, None))\n\n            print(\"Custom Cache Results:\")\n            for lookup, success, member_name in cache_results:\n                status = \"✓\" if success else \"✗\"\n                result = repr(member_name) if success else \"NOT FOUND\"\n                print(f\"  {status} {lookup!r}: {result}\")\n\n            print(\"\\nStandard API Results:\")\n            for lookup, success, member_name in api_results:\n                status = \"✓\" if success else \"✗\"\n                result = repr(member_name) if success else \"NOT FOUND\"\n                print(f\"  {status} {lookup!r}: {result}\")\n\n            cache_success = all(success for _, success, _ in cache_results)\n            api_success = all(success for _, success, _ in api_results)\n\n            print(f\"\\nCache: {'✓ All lookups succeeded' if cache_success else '✗ Some lookups failed'}\")\n            print(f\"API:   {'✓ All lookups succeeded' if api_success else '✗ Some lookups failed'}\")\n\n            return api_success  # The custom cache:\n\n1. Strips trailing path separators from directory member names using removesuffix()\n2. Caches members in a private _ansible_normalized_cache attribute\n3. This approach is fragile because it assumes all directory lookups will be\n   normalized the same way\n\nThe issue occurs when:\n- A tar archive stores directory entries with specific member names\n- The extraction code looks them up using removesuffix() normalization\n- If any lookup uses a different form or if there are edge cases with member\n  storage, the lookup can fail\n\nThe fix is to use the standard tarfile.getmember() API which handles member\nlookups correctly without fragile custom normalization.\n\nRelated Python issue: https://bugs.python.org/issue47231 (now fixed in modern Python)\n\"\"\"\n\nimport json\nimport os\nimport sys\nimport tarfile\nimport tempfile\nfrom io import BytesIO\n\n# Test if we can import the actual ansible code\ntry:\n    sys.path.insert(0, '/app/lib')\n    from ansible.galaxy.collection import install_artifact\n    from ansible.utils.sentinel import Sentinel\n    HAS_ANSIBLE = True\nexcept ImportError as e:\n    print(f\"Warning: Could not import ansible modules: {e}\")\n    HAS_ANSIBLE = False\n\n\ndef create_minimal_collection_tar(tar_path, dir_with_trailing_sep=False):\n    \"\"\"\n    Create a minimal test collection tar file.\n\n    When dir_with_trailing_sep=True, directory entries will have trailing separators.\n    This is the edge case that can trigger bugs in the custom cache approach.\n    \"\"\"\n    with tarfile.open(tar_path, mode='w:gz') as tar:\n        # The custom cache:\n\n1. Strips trailing path separators from directory member names using removesuffix()\n2. Caches members in a private _ansible_normalized_cache attribute\n3. This approach is fragile because it assumes all directory lookups will be\n   normalized the same way\n\nThe issue occurs when:\n- A tar archive stores directory entries with specific member names\n- The extraction code looks them up using removesuffix() normalization\n- If any lookup uses a different form or if there are edge cases with member\n  storage, the lookup can fail\n\nThe fix is to use the standard tarfile.getmember() API which handles member\nlookups correctly without fragile custom normalization.\n\nRelated Python issue: https://bugs.python.org/issue47231 (now fixed in modern Python)\n\"\"\"\n\nimport json\nimport os\nimport sys\nimport tarfile\nimport tempfile\nfrom io import BytesIO\n\n# Test if we can import the actual ansible code\ntry:\n    sys.path.insert(0, '/app/lib')\n    from ansible.galaxy.collection import install_artifact\n    from ansible.utils.sentinel import Sentinel\n    HAS_ANSIBLE = True\nexcept ImportError as e:\n    print(f\"Warning: Could not import ansible modules: {e}\")\n    HAS_ANSIBLE = False\n\n\ndef create_minimal_collection_tar(tar_path, dir_with_trailing_sep=False):\n    \"\"\"\n    Create a minimal test collection tar file.\n\n    When dir_with_trailing_sep=True, directory entries will have trailing separators.\n    This is the edge case that can trigger bugs in the custom cache approach.\n    \"\"\"\n    with tarfile.open(tar_path, mode='w:gz') as tar:\n        # The custom cache:\n\n1. Strips trailing path separators from directory member names using removesuffix()\n2. Caches members in a private _ansible_normalized_cache attribute\n3. This approach is fragile because it assumes all directory lookups will be\n   normalized the same way\n\nThe issue occurs when:\n- A tar archive stores directory entries with specific member names\n- The extraction code looks them up using removesuffix() normalization\n- If any lookup uses a different form or if there are edge cases with member\n  storage, the lookup can fail\n\nThe fix is to use the standard tarfile.getmember() API which handles member\nlookups correctly without fragile custom normalization.\n\nRelated Python issue: https://bugs.python.org/issue47231 (now fixed in modern Python)\n\"\"\"\n\nimport json\nimport os\nimport sys\nimport tarfile\nimport tempfile\nfrom io import BytesIO\n\n# Test if we can import the actual ansible code\ntry:\n    sys.path.insert(0, '/app/lib')\n    from ansible.galaxy.collection import install_artifact\n    from ansible.utils.sentinel import Sentinel\n    HAS_ANSIBLE = True\nexcept ImportError as e:\n    print(f\"Warning: Could not import ansible modules: {e}\")\n    HAS_ANSIBLE = False\n\n\ndef create_minimal_collection_tar(tar_path, dir_with_trailing_sep=False):\n    \"\"\"\n    Create a minimal test collection tar file.\n\n    When dir_with_trailing_sep=True, directory entries will have trailing separators.\n    This is the edge case that can trigger bugs in the custom cache approach.\n    \"\"\"\n    with tarfile.open(tar_path, mode='w:gz') as tar:\n        # extraction fragility.\n\nThis test demonstrates the issue with the custom normalized tar member cache\nintroduced as a workaround for a CPython tarfile bug. The custom cache:\n\n1. Strips trailing path separators from directory member names using removesuffix()\n2. Caches members in a private _ansible_normalized_cache attribute\n3.
